\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/2d8adbbfe6610df97852fafcdb869054.png}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Recently on a visit to my kid's doctor appointment, I rediscovered this toy I loved. My favorite way of playing with these was grabbing the bottom-most block and swooping it around from one end of the toy to the other. It was always so satisfying feeling it bring the rest of the blocks along for the ride.This made me think about habit stacking from the book, "The Power of Habit". This was a first draft of the idea and I hope to refine it in a future post. 😊
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Beginner's Mind and Finding Clarity}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-08}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/88fed55bf7c04e9b80d33e30c706f162.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The secret sauce to solving difficult problems is combining the efficiency of the expert with the openness of a beginners mind.There’s tremendous value in specialization and expertise.But there's also a hidden trap.To become an expert, you have to zoom in and learn deeply about a singular domain. The more you do something, the more efficient you get. But as you specialize and your efficiency improves, your attention gets narrower and you lose the ability to think laterally.Said another way, when you become an expert you sacrifice creativity for efficiency. The visual above celebrates the beginner's mind, or \textit{shoshin }(初心) as its known in Japanese Zen Buddhism. In the context of Zen, a beginner’s mind is like when you eat something for the very first time. Imagine that first bite. Its taste. Its texture. Its aroma...fully immersed in each moment of that experience. Having a beginner's mind is about: • snapping yourself out of auto-pilot mode• sustaining curiosity• and checking your assumptions about what's possible.

\textbf{DIVE DEEPER: }My favorite real world example of this is the the case of the scientist who discovered H. Pylori.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Beginner's Mind and Finding Clarity}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-08}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/06da478c5e162eb9e66926399b395f6d.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Had so much fun drawing this, especially figuring out how to create the illusion of shaking up the globe.

When it’s manageable, anxiety and tension can help motivate you towards dreams and aspirations.But if you feel a paralyzing chaos welling up daily, I’d invite you to start a journaling practice to calm the mind and settle the soul.Journaling can be more than an inventory of the events of the day. It can be a method to reflect on what's going on internally and become more consciously aware of what you're feeling.Any kind of reflection is helpful, but I’m a proponent of journaling by hand because it helps you slow down and take note of what you're experiencing.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Beginner's Mind and Finding Clarity}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-08}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/cabfc77005ddd09f821a3eeab3b3b602.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
As a teacher, an analogy is the most effective way to communicate foreign concepts. I came up with this one as I backed out of the driveway thinking about how to explain why my students should write to clarify their thinking about what they wanted to achieve for the year. I'm flattered to have been DM'd several times over the last couple months asking about my process of coming up with visuals. It may sound weird, but writing is an essential component of visualization. Without the clarity found through exploring an idea, a visual has no soul. That said, I still feel a deep anxiety with every visual before posting, wondering "Is This Anything?"[affiliate link] much like Jerry Seinfeld thinks before a joke.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Cycle of Growth and Stoic Philosophy}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f635d99b631a1ba5ff075e5cce550266.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This image made it to the Interesting slot because it's the first image I posted where I received a ton of feedback on the analogy itself (which I love actually because it forces me to improve my thinking and iterate the drawing).

For me, the key idea is when you're working on something alone, the low-hanging fruit is the easiest to grab.

But if you want a sweeter reward, getting there in a team is easier, even if the fruit (🥁) of that labor may need to be shared.

Honestly though...working together with a community toward a goal is more fun and better for the spirit.

I imagine the characters in this picture cracking up as they try not to topple over one another. 😂

\textbf{Artist's Note:} Iteration for Clarity• Include all three of the characters grabbing low-hanging fruit with three golden apples at the top. • When they're grabbing the fruit on the right, "Bluey" will have a basket full of 2 golden apples as he holds the third.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Cycle of Growth and Stoic Philosophy}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/9e1499116ca07159c80fe7ac38143f71.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
99\% of people who embrace a growth mindset fall into the trap thinking there's a singular moment when they'll be...well...fully grown (AKA good at the thing).

But this is a mistake.

\textbf{Growth is a cycle,} not a destination.

You're playing an infinite game. Enjoy the swim.

\textbf{Artist's Note: }I saw this weird looking circle in one of my kid's children's books. It got me thinking about this birds eye shot of an ocean with this image of a guy swimming around and around, lap by lap, hour by hour, with no goal but to keep swimming. If I drew this in my 20s, I'd probably draw the guy swimming the whole cycle through. But being in my 40s now, I see the value of rest and how it contributes to a more solid lasting foundation of growth.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Cycle of Growth and Stoic Philosophy}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/addeba8703ded30b901e0d18cf244283.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Inspired by one of my favorite ideas of Stoicism illustrated most eloquently in this line:

“The impediment to action advances action. What stands in the way becomes the way.”

How you perceive the obstacles in your life defines your path forward.

The obstacle isn't a bug. It's the feature.

\textbf{Artist's Note:} This idea came to me when I was looking at my staircase. When I looked straight at them, the tiling made it look as if one stair blended into the next! It got me thinking...this is actually quite dangerous...😅
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{I.D.E.A. Newsletter 9: Storytelling and Comfort Zones}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-22}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/4d0110068e4ee382f4b22ff2562e5d05.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The highlight of my week was when my friend @EvansNifty posted this visual demonstrating my philosophy on storytelling.

If you want your content to stand out, involve the audience as active participants of your work.Telling a good story is as if you're drawing a circle for your audience.

But instead of forming the circle completely by yourself, you want to leave it slightly incomplete.

That small gap at the end is for the audience to complete themselves.

Don't give the audience the answer (4). Engage them with the question (2+2).
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{I.D.E.A. Newsletter 9: Storytelling and Comfort Zones}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-22}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/998ae232699231de89393e811985d724.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/1707e8138ed61b9220cdd548236b3de6.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The very last lines of "The Practice" by Seth Godin reads:

"The magic is that there is no magic. Start where you're at. Don't Stop."

The top of the Maslow's Hierarchy of Needs pyramid should be changed from "Self-Actualization" to "Continuous Progress."

There's a reason why we begin most movies with our hero in an Ordinary World.

This is the comfort zone.

Soon after our hero's introduced, there's a Call to Action, followed swiftly by the hero's Refusal of the Call.

Why?

Because few people intentionally step into the unknown and into discomfort.

They often have to be pushed into it.

The tragic truth of growth is that it's something we recognize only in hindsight and not as it's happening.

But growth requires us to step into the fray and trust we'll get through to the other side stronger for it.

A flower only grows when it reaches for the sun.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{I.D.E.A. Newsletter 9: Storytelling and Comfort Zones}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-07-22}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/0cfade5a7562e079497b077a3a497a16.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This metaphor tries to tap into multiple different areas and meanings of the words "consuming" and "creating." On face value, consuming is taking from the world, whereas creating is giving back.But also the earth is a finite and fragile resource. We need to drink from it to survive. If we consume without giving back, it will run dry.

Creating a piece of writing, a piece of art, or even a business to serve customers and solve their problems is a generous act.

Be generous. Create something and share it with the world. Give more than you take.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Read More, Build Momentum}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-08-05}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/242257cb6018c6e11fd1192ae5c9660e.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I can't go to the library without checking out at least half the library so I wanted to celebrate the power of reading with this visual.It's true that some skills are impossible to learn by reading alone...like riding a bike or swimming!

But some skills are slow to learn by action alone.

You don't know what you don't know so read more!

\textbf{Artist's Note: }Design is all about problem solving.

If you look at the original post on Twitter, it reads:"READ MORE BOOKS TO GROW" (if read top =\textgreater{} bottom) but some people read it as:"GROW TO BOOKS MORE READ" (bottom =\textgreater{} top). 😅

Why?

The problem is with the visual design 👇🏻
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/deb1d48630b8238064718346cecd9922.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Solution?

Iterate. Come up with 5 words that make sense read forward AND backward:"Step By Step, More Reading," which can also be read:"Reading More, Step by Step."

Not perfect, but better! 💪
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

My depiction of the "flow state."\textbf{Artist's Note:} I was playing with my kids, showing them the slinky-stair trick when this idea came to me. This is the 2nd iteration. You can see the first on my IG.

If you want to make your own visuals, give yourself permission to be imperfect. Know you can make it better with v.2, v.3, and so on till you get the idea right.

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Online Mindsets and Pruning Your Commitments}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-08-23}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/293b49ad4f52a21f0ad68e76c8ec2df1.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The word priority initially meant 1 thing above all others. Having multiple priorities is the same as having no priority.

I might be mixing my metaphors here, but if you plant 10 seeds and ration a cup of water over all 10 seeds, none of them sprout.But if you plant a single seed and use the entire cup to nourish the soil surrounding the seed, it will bear the most delicious of fruits.

When you cut off the excess, you cultivate the space to grow.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Risks, Throbbers, and the Ego!}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-09-06}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/fec72b03a8a2590e95c4dcb486fd5a09.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I made this inspired by Justin Welsh's Saturday Solopreneur newsletter, which was a great reminder to take small bets.

Said another way, take the big thing you're trying to achieve and do a 1\% version of it. (idea from Derek Sivers's book, "Anything You Want.")

If there's anything in your life you've always wanted to do, excavate and execute the 1\% version of it. If there's a big gamble you've been considering, is there a way to make a smaller gamble to test your assumptions?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Risks, Throbbers, and the Ego!}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-09-06}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/fd1bd3dda9cd1c91bf58e98e38d843f3.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
These loading icons are called 'throbbers' (cue high school student snickering). Apple decided to shift from a wristwatch frozen at 9 o'clock (where you're reminded the effect of how you're losing time) to a spinning pinwheel (aka beachball, which was a bit more playful). Of course, we've adapted to the interface and now call it "the spinning wheel of death"...but hey, still a brilliant move in UX design..
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Managing vs Leading \& Life Events vs Storytelling}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-09-20}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/7425d378105c3426c6db0651bea74f45.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
There's a bunch of advice on time management but little on energy management.

To some willpower is grit or the ability to persevere.

To others it's the ability to resist.

For me, it's the discipline to stick to my commitments.

I found if I front-load my day by following through on commitments, I have less anxiety the rest of the day.

I used to be the opposite, but recently I've recognized I'm depleted after dinner and got very little left in the tank.

How do you manage your energy?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

There're lot of books on storytelling, but few have as many practical insights into the artform as Storyworthy.

\small
I am fascinated with how words and labels shift the way we experience the world.

Visuals can help clarify and distill subtle differences in words. Often management and leadership are words used interchangeably but there is a difference.

Both are skills that can be learned.

Both are essential in an organization.

But you should know what you're trying to do and take care to recognize when you should lead and when you need to manage. This was one of my first visuals I posted on Twitter and you can see in my process video, how messy the discovery process of the design and colors were. 😅

\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]

\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The key is to keep the diagonal lines (the red lines) parallel to each other and you'll get perfect perspective when drawing anything that has a pathway and gaps: • railroads, • steps • sidewalks, • bridges, etc. Erase the diagonals at the end and you're good to go. Notice the walls I made are parallel lines going straight up.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

Vanishing Point is most common, but Parallel Perspective is used a lot these days in isometric designs.

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Creative Resistance and Finding Purpose}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-11-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/11f5061c3d3677c03624e5319326bf9d.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Where we place our focus affects the range and depth of our expertise.

As generalists develop range by spreading their focus over many skills, research suggests they are better creative, out-of-the-box thinking, because they see dots from other domains unseen by the specialist.

As specialists develop filling singular skillsets with depth, they are more efficient and can probably better innovate on their given area of expertise.

There're situations where generalists shine and situations where specialists shine.

Where do you stand on the generalist vs specialist argument?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Creative Resistance and Finding Purpose}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-11-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f280f729fbbc1e3d4186e96ec570bd06.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I love using shadows in my work. They increase the overall turnaround time of finishing each illustration, but they're not just for looks. They're a practical tool to add to your tool belt for conveying space and where objects are in relativity to one another.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Creative Resistance and Finding Purpose}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-11-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/26dac188294a878b3dc2c2100ab52279.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
“Resistance will tell you anything to keep you from doing your work.”

Resistance is sneaky because it's always present.

It's like the proverbial fish in David Foster Wallace's now famous commencement speech, "This is Water."

If you've never heard it, here's an excerpt:

"There are these two young fish swimming along and they happen to meet an older fish swimming the other way, who nods at them and says:

'Morning, boys. How’s the water?'

And the two young fish swim on for a bit, and then eventually one of them looks over at the other and goes:

'What the hell is water?'"

-David Foster Wallace

Resistance is our water. It's the default. It slows progress.

But it's completely possible to push through to the other side.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Creative Resistance and Finding Purpose}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-11-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/1bf0058cadea3b6c64856d11ad3f3aae.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
"Passion brings immediate joy.

Values provide lasting meaning."

There's something about the fuel a purpose-driven life provides that helps forge our hearts to be more resilient.

If you can somehow melt the two together, then you'll be able to sustain your mission even when the immediate burst of joy has burnt out.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

I felt compelled to simplify these graphs, which I admit are sobering (even depressing) but they're also eye-opening.

Please be sure to check out the reminders under each image.

\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How Americans Spend Time and Shiny Object Syndrome}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-12-06}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/1d538845a41e5626e20c4afcd48b5052.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Write between the lines. (this visual took me ages to get right)
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How Americans Spend Time and Shiny Object Syndrome}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2022-12-06}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a580fc45ca634d7de2253562ba53e9ac.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Shiny object syndrome} is when you're constantly jumping from project to project because you think the next new thing is going to bring more value than the current thing.

It's essentially thinking "the grass is greener on the other side" and then hopping from one lawn to the next in search of the greenest grass. The irony is that the reason the grass is greener somewhere else is because you never stay long enough where you are to take care of it.

I have such a problem with shiny object syndrome. I do it with books, with hobbies, even with cleaning the house (much to my wife's irritation).

Recently I'm learning how to leverage my focus for deeper value. And any time I've been able to stay focused and dive deep on one thing, I find not only actual results, but deeper fulfillment because I \textit{feel} the progress.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Collecting Ideas vs. Creating Outcomes}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-02-08}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/774fbbca0f14196baff2dbd82a88f0d4.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The Unsuspecting Balloon Metaphor} is a classic. The key to doing this one well is to reveal something the audience is not expecting that's a threat to what they want. Bonus points for specificity.Classic Example: \textbf{Positive Desired Outcome:} Ability to Focus\textbf{Non-obvious Thread:} A Single Notification
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Collecting Ideas vs. Creating Outcomes}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-02-08}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/25f11ffd5e92a861cf854e0e59b28a27.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Collecting Ideas vs. Creating Outcomes}There's a concept called the collector's fallacy:

Believing that by collecting information, we somehow absorb it.

It gives us a false sense of progress.

There's nothing wrong with reading for pleasure. But if you're reading to learn how to do something, there's no substitute for action. I hesitated putting my work online for years because I didn't know 'exactly' what I wanted to do.

Finally started posting in March '22 and things started happening. Real progress is made only through behavior and action.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Collecting Ideas vs. Creating Outcomes}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-02-08}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/5332b6a92259c9472debe33fe252bb45.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{"Reading is essential for those who seek to rise above the ordinary."}-Jim Rohn
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Fluid vs Crystalized Intelligence}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-03-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/5d6dff56e22281550173223d586e5cbc.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I've been thinking about age a lot recently so I was intrigued to come across the above concept from Catell's Intelligence Theory. Apparently, many physicists, scientists, and even entrepreneurs hit their innovation peak early in their careers. And they waste the latter end of their lives miserable because they continue to chase success to rival that of their youth. Turns out, there's a scientific reason for this inability.

There're two types of intelligence (and they're affected by age).

\textbf{Fluid Intelligence:} Ability to solve problems by coming up with new innovative ways to attack the problem. Peaks somewhere between ages 20-25 and then slowly declines afterward.

\textbf{Crystalized Intelligence:} Ability to solve problems from accumulated knowledge (make connections). This grows stronger with age.

The problem comes when people neglect making the jump from fluid intelligence to leverage crystallized intelligence during midlife. Important to note, these intelligences are not related to IQ.

From the book: "From Strength to Strength" by Arthur C. Brooks. (amazon link)
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Fluid vs Crystalized Intelligence}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-03-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/958a1b03244bee19854c1f7ae2ef4c5f.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
For this week's template, we're tapping into UX which is a valuable inspiration for visual thinking.

Example: "It's time to work out." Choice 1: "LET'S GO" Choice 2: "Snooze"

In the above example, the question is optional (it can even be a declarative sentence or a warning signal). It's just used to frame the context of the choice.

Note where the mouse is. You can hover it over a choice to nudge your audience to one of the choices. Alternatively, you can hover the mouse in the middle to let your audience decide.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\textbf{Hofstadter's Law }is helpful to consider when planning for something. It states that we always underestimate how long it'll take to complete a task, even when we're conscious of Hofstadter's Law.

This law has single-mindedly targeted me all my life. 😂

\small
\textbf{The water you drink affects the ideas you think.}

As with all my visuals, there're elements of personal experience embedded in the image. For me:

Netflix - consumed me instead of me consuming it. (I felt like my watch list was a to-do list!)

TikTok - there's educational content but it's really difficult to be intentional in this format for me.

News - I have personally not been inspired to create anything after watching the news. It usually paralyzes me with despair.

We fuel or pollute our creative well with the content we consume. Curious, what fuels (or pollutes) you to be inspired to create something?
\end{minipage}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Mental Models and Setting a Priority}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-03-28}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b6c2b0898b7571285b59d2fadc0fdc55.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I've been diving more into visualizing mental models as they apply to visual thinking (also applies in writing).

Here's how to use \textbf{Occam's Razor. }

• Choose the simplest explanation• Remove distracting details• Keep only the essential

Why use it?• Increases clarity• Amplifies your message• Simplifies your approach
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Mental Models and Setting a Priority}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-03-28}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/eec9e59002d6f25abefb63eb77ba0210.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This is one framework I use myself pretty regularly. It's a template communicating a \textbf{comparison in quantity}, similar to a pie chart.

\textbf{Important note:} As with any visual, the most important thing is to communicate the difference and not the exact numbers. In my work, I focus on communicating the spirit of the idea. I am not so much creating a data visualization.

Here's an example of it in action:

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Telephoto Thinking vs Wide-Angle Thinking}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-04-11}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/badb981bf35963e6f26bb34abc3d301e.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Which are you--a telephoto or wide-angle lens thinker?}

Most people want to be both (variable lens) but if forced to choose, I'd say most starting online content creators lean toward generalists.

The thing about telephoto lenses is that they're extremely difficult to focus unless you place them on a stable footing. This feels in line with how most creatives feel when they're told to niche down and specialize if they want to develop an identity to be recognized online.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Telephoto Thinking vs Wide-Angle Thinking}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-04-11}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/4d4d7a731fc4414a07498017838ab9f7.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{"It gets easier" Design. }

The goal of this design is to change the perception of what seems impossible at first. Essentially create progressively smaller versions of a symbol representing what you want to convey getting easier over time.
\end{minipage}

Unfortunately, getting older means also feeling the inevitable loss of the people we love most. And each time feels like the first.

In these moments, I find myself feeling tremendous guilt and shame. Guilt if I try to live a life without them and shame I didn't do more when they were alive.

There's a beautiful TED talk I was reminded of recently off a grief post from Michael J. Boorman (@wisdommadeeasy) that we don't ever really move on from grief. We move forward with it.

A quote I think about that helps me move forward with grief:

"What is grief if not love persevering?"

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Hard Decisions and the Clarity of Humility}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-05-02}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8da9bf15f767b0c1cfc0af1726d5dbca.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Beware the path of least resistance. \\
Careful walking the fine line between thoughtful reflection and willful procrastination as the urgent often overshadows the important.\\
Read the full post here.

I had an interesting comment to this visual on LinkedIn. Specifically, that on the opposite side of “Pain” should be the word “Pleasure.” I respectfully disagreed. The absence of pain is not necessarily pleasure. 

What do you think?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Hard Decisions and the Clarity of Humility}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-05-02}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/2750da5366f1b38fefb6b1e8bcdff7c1.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This visual uses a \textbf{“This to That” Framework}. All that means is comparing \textbf{this} (fear in imagination) to \textbf{that} (fear in reality). It’s a simple but powerful device to help you frame something in context.

Couple this with one of my favorite creative levers to pull: \textit{exaggeration}.

Exaggeration can help you interpret an idea specifically to your own point of view.

Be careful though. Exaggeration is a double-edged sword in visual thinking. An exaggerated analogy may have more difficulty getting your message across because a more literal audience might get stuck in saying, “It’s not really like that.”
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Hard Decisions and the Clarity of Humility}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-05-02}
\vspace*{\fill}

{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}

\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a5a9179e83c9e0d66ecd508f0305d102.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Name and recognize failures, but focus more on ingraining the lessons they teach you.

Let temporary setbacks wash away.
\end{minipage}

How will we look at these tools 20 years from now?

Every corner of the internet is buzzing with “AI this” or “AI that.” 😵‍💫

I’m still working out how I feel about it as a teacher. but love it or hate it, it’s here to stay. I wonder if people will one day look at AI-assisted writing in English class the we way we look at calculators in Math.

On the other hand:

\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f4bccdc24537d9b0b6cf175e8bc9325e.png}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{It is the cracked pot that lets the light in.}\\
-Leonard Cohen

Not a direct quote, but a paraphrased one.

This image drew up some challenging comments on Instagram. A few people remarked how they were betrayed by revealing too much to the people they trusted.

This reminded me how I’ve been burned too, more times than I can count. In fact, the one thing I remember from my dad growing up is how many times his friends swindled him out of his hard-earned money because he revealed too many scars, which created real fears in me around trust.

But I’ve also been lucky to meet people who restored some of that trust. \\
• An art teacher who encouraged me out of a sea of 4,000 other low-income, public school students to keep creating. \\
• An elderly Japanese man in Hiroshima who saw me lost in the train station and spent 2 hours to help me get to where I was going. \\
• A friend I just met in Thailand inviting me over to share in Christmas dinner and presents so I wouldn’t spend the holidays alone.

Some scars heal and some scars fester. All I know is I saw what the festering did to my dad and that’s something I’d like to avoid.

I’m curious, how do you navigate revealing who you are on social media?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to get the morning gunk out of your head}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-06-20}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/336a3df0f51023ce33f1440a740f4ca8.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Clear your mind for the day.

Inspired by the concept of Morning Pages from the book The Artist’s Way by Julia Cameron. But honestly, any-time journaling is better than nothing. 

I have one on hand whenever and wherever I go to 'process' and get the gunk out. 🤓
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

So back to the drawing board (🥁)

My first attempt

• Reads top-down and left-to-right, so problem = growth mindset is seen first

• Red graph dominates the image

• Thought bubbles make less sense

• Helps me identify the central problem = Reveal each element so it can be read in the correct order

Below is the final version solving the central design problem. Curious, how might you have solved this differently?

— Epictetus, Discourses, 2.5.4–5

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Growth Minded Celebrations and Disagreements}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-07-04}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
One of the most common issues creators face when visual thinking is speed of execution. The main reason for this is a lack of a system to help avoid falling in the trap of “pixel pushing.” 

I do two simple things that help me speed up my workflow and make it less likely I waste my design time on moving elements around:

1) Brainstorm on LARGE sheets paper (I use 11×17) or a journal (my notebook of choice if interested) \textbf{with a pen} because:\\
• No way to erase forces efficiency and an attitude of imperfection\\
• Having a large canvas allows for multiple iterations on the same page

2) Design on Canva to get a sense of where things should go. \\
• Canva can be a great free tool to test how things will look with colors and design\\
• Can speed up getting sizing and proportions of different elements without worrying about drawing 

Here’s a before and after of a cheeky version of the productivity jar meme I made this weekend.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3f32fd57ed485e7fbe63e01388968b2e.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Layout done in Canva
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\begin{center}

\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ec2d11376a50b5b95ed8fafa2a1248ea.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Deadbolt Mindset vs Blue Sky Mindset

When I disagree with someone, I often assume I already know what they’re gonna say before they say it. This approach has rarely if ever helped me resolve an issue. 

So over the last several months, I’ve made a concerted effort to prompt myself to stay curious in arguments (helps a lot in relationship squabbles).

I simply do this through asking questions. What’s critical (and didn’t initially come natural to me), is avoiding leading or rhetorical questions. They’re only helpful if they’re earnest questions.

Login or Subscribe to participate
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Setbacks and Sheeran's Law}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-08-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b953a0872accb3dc6bb6f2a178a996bf.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Sheeran's Law \\
("Rule of the Dirty Faucet)

A piece of advice I give my screenwriting students:\\
Write ALL your ideas down.

Especially the bad ones.

If you leave it, the gunk expands and muddies your thinking.

If you want to make the good stuff, you have to get through the bad stuff.

"When you switch on the dirty tap, sh*t water is going to flow out for a substantial amount of time. Then clean water is gonna start flowin'”\\
-Ed Sheeran
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Setbacks and Sheeran's Law}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-08-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
There’s a lot that goes into \textbf{clarifying}, \textbf{simplifying} and \textbf{amplifying} an idea and turning into a visual, but ask any creator and they’ll tell you it all starts with writing down observations.

Sounds simple enough.

But one important principle most people forget:\\
\textbf{Delay judgement }until you’re in the execution phase.

One thing I tell my students all the time is \textit{“brainstorming is an idea generation process, not a decision making one.” }

Here’s one of my original notes:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ba6e65ca8fbe885761902f18cf82fd47.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Not pretty I know but I try to make it a point to draw an idea from my head in less than 10 seconds in notes. 

This observation later turned into this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ef540b5d7078d7a3bb2eccfa0a17d5b3.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Takeaways:}

Write all ideas and observations down without judging their merit.

Challenge yourself to getting it on the page in less than 10s.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Maximizing vs Optimizing Your Day}

{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]

\begin{center}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Maximizing your schedule vs optimizing your schedule.

I first started thinking about this when I heard James Clear, author of “Atomic Habits,” speak on the Tim Ferris show.

He asks, when thinking about how to manage your time, \textbf{“what are you optimizing for?”}

Instead of trying to maximize your days, be a little more at peace with…well…living an optimized life unique for you.

If you’re interested in exploring these ideas further, I’d highly recommend these 2 books:

“4000 Weeks”
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\small
A question from a student \textbf{in my course}: \\
\textbf{How do you build a consistent looking brand from visual to visual? }

I wish I had a good hack…but it took me some time. Below are my first 50ish visuals I ever posted.

When I first started, I did my best to actually avoid worrying about style or consistency (as you might be able to tell from the images below). But a funny thing happened after doing it for a couple months…I started getting messages saying specifically how they liked my style! 🤯

And surprisingly, around mid-July 2022 (about 4 months and 50+ visuals after I started), you can see the style I use today emerging out of the pack.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/207e4a66ce09bd435e4244f91be4b33b.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e5781bcea64dc5808e70829bcdb27f58.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/790e099f8e93a81f4889d7ff1f30ef8a.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/9e3e74f1a336c86f6a8bc78749fb7aea.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/858a1287c0c876dece0c25acd86315a3.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The lesson?

In the beginning, it’s more important to make stuff to see what you like and what’s working. Style inevitably emerges (whether you mean to or not 😅) and it evolves with your practice.

Style is more than just colors and fonts. It’s about voice and the kinds of messages you hope to portray.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{A system to capture ideas and organizing chaos with storytelling}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-09-12}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/cb8677d622a81faf7efe5b2367569ec5.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Inspired by Tiago Forte and \textbf{his book, “Building a Second Brain.”}

A \textit{second brain} is a fancy word for an intentional notetaking system that keeps tracks of your ideas, projects, and other efforts in your life.

I have a bit of a convoluted process but it works for me:

\textbf{Quick Capture:} Drafts or Apple Notes (fleeting ideas in day)

\textbf{Slow Capture:} Notebook \& Pen (journal \& sketch)

\textbf{Long Capture:} Obsidian (examining \& colliding ideas)

The most important thing is not 'how', but 'how long.'

Avoid the temptation to switch systems once you’ve made a couple decisions. Stick to a system long enough to work out the kinks so it works for you.

There's no perfect system. It just becomes less imperfect over time. ❤️
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{A system to capture ideas and organizing chaos with storytelling}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-09-12}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A simple tip for communicating ideas visually: \\
Use ❌ and ✅ to communicate your point of view.

What’s the number one thing your visual metaphor should answer?

That’s right!

The \textbf{Call to Action}!

In my \textbf{maximizing vs optimizing visual}\textbf{, }I present a difference…but then…

…what am I asking the reader to consider once they’ve seen this distinction?

That’s where I can say ❌ \textbf{(avoid this)}, but instead ✅ \textbf{(do this)}!

How cool is that?! 🤓
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/7bb458ec3f6653cb7cb47fdec6f1055f.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Before
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{A system to capture ideas and organizing chaos with storytelling}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-09-12}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/0823c7ce1446d9148c87f68d276d7c74.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
In my 20th year teaching film and animation…

Wanna know the most difficult challenge my students face?

Learning to write economically. Saying more with less.

The process starts with throwing up everything onto the first draft (in screenwriting, we call this the “vomit script”…I restrained myself from visualizing this 🤣)

Then, compress as much as possible and squeeze out any excess crud!

\end{minipage}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The difference between thinking and overthinking}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The difference between thinking and overthinking. Stay sharp!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The difference between thinking and overthinking}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-09-26}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
If you don’t already have a sketchbook, consider starting one. 

\textbf{PRO TIP:} Use the same notebook to sketch and journal. Written insights inspire visual insights and vice versa.

\textbf{Law of Ideation}

\textit{Take your idea and make it real, no matter how rough. The final step is only attainable by taking the first step. }

One of my favorite creative practices is sketching visual strategies.

\textbf{What’s a visual strategy?} \\
It’s how an artist solves an idea problem with a visual solution.

For instance, the visual strategy below from the talented Wang Wei-Shen shows a possible solution to the problem: what happens when you cross a threshold.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e4501303039c34891f93620af8c6b57e.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Initial capture in my notebook. You might be able to see echoes of my journaling on the other side of the page.

This sketch ended up motivating the visual below on the left, which then iterated to the version on the right.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/2aadc144dbb14228079e7cd74dd212ae.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/2f4d836a93e1ae9b0b465738675a3ff5.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
But you know what’s funny?

I only realized this sketch was the source of inspiration months later. It burned into my subconscious image bank without my knowing. That’s the power of a strong capture habit.

Creative output is fueled by creative input.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The Lines in Sand Effect:}\\
A simple mental model to get past overthinking and the fear of making decisions.

Any time I’ve had to make a choice where I recognize I’m procrastinating because of the fear of making a mistake, I imagine this metaphor.

I’ve done this to decide:

niches

type of clients I serve

tech platforms

even habits \& routines

It comforts me to remind myself these decisions aren’t set it stone.

Login or Subscribe to participate
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{2 Types of Burnout}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-10-10}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d3c342fc707ffcfa87e63aef80783852.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Burning out can happen at 2 intensities:

Most people understand \textbf{“fast burnout”}—when you push yourself beyond capacity towards a goal, sacrificing your physical and mental health.

But equally dangerous is \textbf{“slow burnout”}—when you feel trapped in a situation and your motivation to do anything slowly suffocates. 

We often suffer silently from a misplaced belief that it's all part of "enduring the grind."

To dive deeper, my friend Roberto Ferraro shared this link:

\textbf{Harvard Business Review: }\\
"Is Your Burnout From Too Much Work or Too Little Impact?"
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{2 Types of Burnout}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-10-10}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Most people misunderstand the term “\textbf{steal like an artist.}” They just “steal” and forget the key part of the phrase: \textbf{“like an artist.”}

\textbf{Artists combine.}

An audience should be able to see influence but not a direct carbon copy. \textbf{ }

As Austin Kleon, the author of \textbf{Steal Like an Artist }notes in his book:

“If you steal from one author, it’s plagiarism; if you steal from many, it’s research.”

Here’s a string of influences as an example:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/1a29501342754e2a5ab8755d58f6cdd2.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The above image was influenced by my friend Roberto Ferraro who was originally inspired by combining my illustration of Russian Dolls and an idea from Jeff Mckeon. You can see the evolution of images and thinking.

That’s the power of ‘stealing like an artist.’
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/15429511ba767a3d315fbf7b5d99d6a2.jpeg}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{In the commitment game, speed is your ally (but not in the way you think)}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-10-24}

\begin{center}

\small
"We need to learn the slow 'yes' and the quick 'no.'"\\
-Greg McKeown, author of “Essentialism: The Disciplined Pursuit of Less”

I recognize the word ‘no’ is sometimes a luxury most people in their jobs can’t afford. But we can ask the person making the request to balance out the equation: if we’re going to START doing this, what are we going to STOP doing?
\end{minipage}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{In the commitment game, speed is your ally (but not in the way you think)}

\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The Leaky Bucket Metaphor Framework}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/30dc79f4e9f8526aa93e9a3eac4f23e4.png}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
You can use the Leaky Bucket visual metaphor as a “correction insight”—where you highlight a behavior that may be going overlooked and is preventing a positive outcome.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{In the commitment game, speed is your ally (but not in the way you think)}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-10-24}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}

The older I get, the more I realize how important it is to savor each daily bite of life.

\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{In the commitment game, speed is your ally (but not in the way you think)}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-10-24}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/be1c67c53489565dffbae712c43c679f.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Rocking Horse Syndrome}: Moving a lot, but not progressing. \\
(inspired by Justin Welsh)

Before I had my first kid, I remember reading piles of parenting books \& articles to get prepared for what I knew was gonna be D-Day in the Milani household. (“D” standing for diapers of course 😆)

And you know what? I don’t remember a single piece of advice I read. 

Not a single one.

You know why? They all contradicted each other.

Turns out the only true way to learn parenting is by being a parent. Only then does the advice have a place to be relevant.

It’s the same with business (or probably any skill). Prep all you want, but it’s like using a bike manual to study how to ride a bike. The hope being the first time you get on the bike, you don’t fall.

But everybody falls! In bikes, in parenting, in business.

Time to get on a real horse. Let’s ride.

Login or Subscribe to participate
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Teaching, Breakdowns, True Wealth, \& Insights}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-11-07}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d5e3615459bdbfc8807ca218c5f8574d.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The mediocre teacher tells. }\\
\textbf{The good teacher explains. }\\
\textbf{The superior teacher demonstrates. }\\
\textbf{The great teacher inspires.}\\
-\textbf{ }William Arthur Ward

This illustration about teaching sums up both my teaching philosophy and my creative philosophy.

Instead of feeding someone what to think, I want to leave space to invite them to participate in the meaning.

I’m conscious that makes my work not for everyone…but I hope the people who it is for appreciate the space. 😊
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Teaching, Breakdowns, True Wealth, \& Insights}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-11-07}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Once you understand the relationship you’re presenting in a metaphor, you open the door for your imagination to create substitutions with the same concept.

For example, the iceberg metaphor is considered the most commonly used visual metaphor with the following relationship:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/61c404c5e46dbc29a8bfe65ab06f98ca.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Standard use-case for an iceberg metaphor

Once we understand the above surface vs below surface relationship, we can present it in a different context like this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/7fbb3f280fc0b100379774bb53d82efd.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Can you think of a metaphor using this concept? \\
Shoot me a reply if you do. I’d love to hear it! 

And if you wanna learn more about how to create visual metaphors, \textbf{check out my course, Thinking in Visual Metaphors. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Teaching, Breakdowns, True Wealth, \& Insights}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-11-07}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/4e5298c0b0f65953688f782ed6873a53.png}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Where breakthroughs often come from.}

If I look back at the biggest changes I’ve made in my life, they often took root in times of darkness.

It’s as if you grow more sensitive to the light, because your eyes had to adjust in the dark. It’s unpleasant to be sure…but it’s also no fun staying alone in the dark.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\textbf{There's more than one way to invest in your future.}

I used to think a couple thousand bucks was crazy to pay for some online course…but then I remembered how much it cost to go to college. 😆

And investing time in leveling up your skills is one of the best ways to compound both your wealth of knowledge and your earning potential.

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Habit tracking, comparisons, and why accuracy is overrated}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-11-21}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/636ecfc27c95a03bbba72e20f8fef0e1.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
You've read Atomic Habits. You're convinced.

Systems over goals. Habits over motivation.

Bright eyed, full of hope, you decide tomorrow you're getting it together. And miracle of miracles, you do!

You go by the book. You nail your work out! You think, "why the hell did I wait so long to start?!"

You open your calendar and mark a big X over the day. This must be what Seinfeld was talking about: “Don't break the chain!”

Easy enough.

But 6 days in...you hit a brick wall:\\
• you get sick\\
• you work late\\
• you live a normal day of life when the universe conspires against your best intentions. 

\textbf{Read full post}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Habit tracking, comparisons, and why accuracy is overrated}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-11-21}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{How a simple color change opens the door for your audience to step into imagination}

My kids loved coloring Marvel superheroes growing up. But what’s funny is my son always needed to know EXACTLY what color to use for each character.

Red, white, \& blue for Captain America. \\
Red \& yellow for Iron Man. \\
But when I colored with him, I would use every color of the rainbow.

And of course he’d roll his eyes and say I was doing it wrong.

But I told him I’m just being creative. And he’d stare at me a moment…and just repeat I was wrong 😑 (some lessons take time 😆)

When you express yourself in art, it’s less important to make it accurate and more important to \textbf{make it interesting.}

Make your work unique to you. This can take shape simply in the colors you choose.

Turtles are green. \\
Basketballs are orange. \\
We’ve seen this accuracy in colors thousands of times.

But \textbf{change what your audience expects} and you earn a moment of pause. And pauses are valuable in a noisy world.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/1afb25b6fde30ffd46e0a22b7004e1a3.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The goal is not to portray reality. We can show accurate colors with other mediums and tools.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/52174a5b10a1c0d100c7586b6738d5b9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The goal is to share a sense that this is coming from an imagination. Even a simple color change is a start.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{When you feel lost, think about where you're going}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-12-05}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/2bcf422a2647fc7b577ce853437d6c34.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{"Things which matter most must never be at the mercy of things which matter least." }\\
–Johann Wolfgang von Goethe

One of my biggest “aha” moments came from the book, \textbf{“Essentialism” by Greg Mckeown}.

And the insight was simple: \textbf{the word priority is singular. }

Priority used to mean \textit{“the one thing that’s most important.”}

There was no such thing as priorit\textbf{ies} (plural)!

These days, we all want to do everything, everywhere, all at once. But that’s why we feel spread thin…why we’re everywhere and nowhere!

And personally, I know I often spend far too much time focusing on areas I should never have been in the first place!

Which reminds me of another favorite warning when it comes to where to focus your time:

\textbf{“There is nothing quite so useless, as doing with great efficiency, something that should not be done at all.”}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{When you feel lost, think about where you're going}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-12-05}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
It’s common to get stuck when you’re brainstorming how to visualize an idea. That’s why I have a set of reliable frameworks.

For example, consider the following:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/0458fc1f74df6b8619f5ce614f655f5e.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Inspired by the famous quote from Maya Angelou
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/aca5fa69baacc0e4f42e18cd70f09951.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This framework is inspired by fellow visual creator, Janis Ozolins.

\textbf{Frameworks are thinking vehicles} to get you from point A to point B.

And the more vehicles you know how to drive, the more likely you can travel anywhere you want to go with your messages.

If you want to learn more frameworks like this, you might be interested in the next \textbf{Thinking in Visual Metaphors course}.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{When you feel lost, think about where you're going}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-12-05}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/024f81ca093ec5da5f08264ff4fae777.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Just when you thought you figured it out.}

I loved Rubik’s Cubes as a kid, but honestly I never fully solved one. 😆

Best I could do was solve a single side and mess up everything else in the process.

This typically is my experience when I finally get work stuff in order—the rest of life turns into chaos (health, family, relationships).

P.S. My son can solve a Rubik’s Cube in less than 26 seconds…there’s a lesson in there somewhere. 🤔

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How expertise hurts your creativity and the ancient Zen Buddhist mindset that changes it}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2023-12-19}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/c9b024bb932aaba345699a745ef657f6.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The definition of integrity. }

One of my favorite things to journal on is defining what a word means to me.

I started doing this after studying for the GRE (a test students have to take in the states to go to graduate school).

It made me realize there were lots of words I knew how to use in a sentence, but could only explain vaguely.

For example, take a simple word like “love”.

If you’ve ever read \textbf{The Five Love Languages}, then you know people have different (often subconscious) ways they define love.

And if you define what love means to you and see how it aligns with your partner’s definition, it’s pretty helpful to communicate more effectively in your relationship.

In the same vein, I’ve found clarifying how you understand other vague words (like integrity) helps align a deeper relationship with yourself.

I’m curious, is your definition of integrity the same or different?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How fixing what's broke is not about knowing what to do}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-02}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/bc882005892740c73ae00766ed15eab8.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
If you want to be more creative, give your ideas time to hatch.

A common mistake I see my students make is giving up too soon.

Try this next time you’re stuck:

go for a walk in silence

take a coffee break

let your subconscious bake your ideas!

This is the Law of Incubation.

Inspired by \textbf{Joey Cofone's book: Laws of Creativity.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How fixing what's broke is not about knowing what to do}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-02}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Clear, Not Clever}

When designing a visual metaphor, one of the most important elements to nail down is the labels you use.

Labels are words, arrows, even punctuation that communicate what the metaphor is.

And the key to using effective labels is clarity. Clarity is step 1 of \textbf{my 3-Step framework to making a visual}.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/c98fa1468cc374dab1f9b70f931c1bd6.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
What’s critical to remember—clarity is about removing as much friction as possible between you and your audience to get your message across.

(And that means you can’t hide behind fancy words if your message is unclear to begin with)

When you write in a fancy way to impress people, you make them do extra work just so you can seem cool

This issue of Visual I.D.E.A.s is sponsored by Superside:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How we frame failure paves our road to success}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-16}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/28f2ba379c0f25f5b675e15ffa6db341.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The mental model that stops me from having an opinion about everything:

\textbf{Dunning-Kruger Effect}--\\
The less you know, the less you question.\\
The more you know, the more you question everything.

I’m fascinated by self-deception and our lack of awareness of how we think and make decisions. And the Dunning-Kruger Effect is a self-deception we all can fall prey to…because well, you don’t know what you don’t know.

One of my goals this year is to reread (and take notes this time!) the book, \textbf{“Thinking Fast and Thinking Slow” by Daniel Kahneman, }because it’s mentioned in practically every book on psychology and sociology ever written since it’s inception. Watch this space for more visuals on cognitive biases 👀
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How we frame failure paves our road to success}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-16}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
In the last couple weeks I’ve posted a few more process timelapse videos on how I make my visuals.

You might observe \textbf{my process} \textbf{is messy…}and that’s because there’s no better cure for a perfectionist than to let chaos reign! I gave myself permission to be messy 2 years ago when I started making visuals.

I wanted to allow myself to work out ideas through the act of making the thing, not thinking about making the thing.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8e6607662f41d782005a20d0225ef631.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
One thing you’ll notice in my videos is I write as I draw. This is important when creating visual metaphors since the labels are a critical part of the meaning.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/61b77be40e7f10992e2b55243fdb5e3d.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8aa2ce386730545ac76fa537fafa137a.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Which brings up the piece of advice I’d like to leave you today when you’re working through a problem. \textbf{Write ALL ideas down}. Especially the bad ones.

\textbf{Bad ideas are like pinballs that bounce around in your head till you get it out. }Often it’s not till you take the bad ideas out of your head that there’s enough space for the good ideas to rise to the surface!

Cohort 3 of \textbf{Thinking in Visual Metaphors }is live! And it’s the biggest cohort I’ve hosted yet but still keeping it nice and cozy! 🙌
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/254b65ca23ba95fc2a22c4fcde79d890.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
My favorite comment from the cohort so far: \\
\textbf{“It is possible to get started and get going without advanced drawing skills.”}\\
-Kalyana

If you’re curious to learn how to make visual metaphors, you can \textbf{sign up for the waitlist for the next cohort here}. \textbf{ }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The simple shift in my thinking that got me started posting online}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-30}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8da1dfc21e282da50dc5c5662a6618f2.png}

\small
A large portion of the visuals I create are \textbf{“Friendly Reminders”} to not only the people who support my work, but to myself. They echo ideas we know to be true, but are lost in the noise of everyday distractions.

This piece highlights the 3 areas in Milani Creative I’m focusing on in 2024.

\textbf{What are you hoping to do less of (more of) this year?}
