\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The simple shift in my thinking that got me started posting online}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-30}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Today’s design tip is more of an encouragement.

An encouragement to remember—we all start somewhere.

For all the aspiring writers, artists, and creators out there: I’d like to share one of my favorite pieces on the creative struggle from the creator of “This American Life” podcast, Ira Glass:

“Nobody tells this to people who are beginners…

All of us who do creative work, we get into it because we have good taste. \textbf{But there is this gap. }

For the first couple years you make stuff, it’s just not that good.

It’s trying to be good. \\
It has potential. \\
But it’s not.

But your taste, the thing that got you into the game, is still killer. \\
And \textbf{your taste is why your work disappoints you. }

A lot of people never get past this phase. They quit…We all go through this.

And if you are just starting out or you are still in this phase, you gotta know \textbf{its normal} and the most important thing you can do is \textbf{do a lot of work.}”

Which inspired this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/79b24c2feb3455a8a2bc02e75744698a.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I’d highly recommend listening to the full quote (it’s short) and watching this\textbf{ beautiful short film that visualizes it}. I show it to all my high school students who want to step into the creative arena to do battle!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The simple shift in my thinking that got me started posting online}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-30}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/2ca107ddae4b21d6c581b103b30c809c.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The growth mindset is an infinite game.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The simple shift in my thinking that got me started posting online}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-01-30}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d51e292bbe9202c33b028cb941941bb9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
In many ways, this visual is connected to “The Gap” idea above.

I procrastinated posting online for over a decade. I kept thinking I’d get started as soon as I knew exactly what I wanted to do. And I didn’t want to post “crap.” I wanted my stuff to be good!

Turns out…this was a great strategy to get older, but not wiser.

I didn’t do anything—for literally over a decade! Because the sad truth was I had no idea what “good” was and what “crap” was.

But then I read a book by Derek Sivers called \textbf{“Anything You Want: 40 Lessons for a New Kind of Entrepreneur.” }

And I came across the following excerpt:

“If you want to be useful, you can always start now, with only 1 percent of what you have in your grand vision.

It'll be a humble prototype version of your grand vision, but you'll be in the game.

You'll be ahead of the rest, because you actually started, while others are waiting for the finish line to magically appear at the starting line.“

This one idea became my action manifesto.

\textbf{Take the small bet version before putting all your chips on the table. }

Test first, double down what works.

It lifted the paralysis that kept me from progressing…for over a decade!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What most people get wrong about iteration and change}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-02-13}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I have to remind myself of this idea everyday:

\textbf{The choices you make every day matter. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/89825126d1bd6ee488c4cba032b8bddf.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/43370857b5a4ea6f557287991c787ce7.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The snowball compounding impact of daily decisions is challenging to wrap our heads around (especially when we make decisions in the counter direction we’re aiming for).

Recently I’ve been falling into the “I’ll do better tomorrow” trap…especially with diet.

My kryptonite—chocolate chip cookies…and guess what they serve everyday at the school cafeteria? 😅

“Surely this cookie today isn’t that big of a deal,” I catch myself saying for the 3rd week in a row…

What are you working towards this season? I’d love to hear! \\
(I may not always get a chance to reply but I read every email ❤️)

\textbf{1\% better: 1.01}\textbf{365 }\textbf{= 37.78}\\
\textbf{1\% worse: 0.99}\textbf{365 }\textbf{= 0.03}

Inspired by the book, \textbf{“Atomic Habits” by James Clear}\\
*I reread James Clear’s article on this idea regularly: \textbf{Continuous Improvement: How It Works and How to Master It.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What most people get wrong about iteration and change}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-02-13}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I’ve spoken before about the importance of iteration to bridge the gap between your ability and taste.

Today, I want to illustrate (🥁) \textbf{a common mistake} people make when they iterate: \textbf{focusing too heavily on “improving” the image}.

Of course we want the image to be better, but starting with that mindset actually blocks the creative process.

I tell my students all the time that \textbf{brainstorming is idea generation, not decision making. }

Starting with improvement in mind is decision making before the ideas have generated.

❌ how can I improve it? (explores only ideas you assume are good)\\
✅ how can articulate this idea in another way? (lets in all ideas, good and bad—we want ALL ideas to flow in our stream of consciousness)

\textbf{Improving is more a byproduct of trying out different articulations.}

Take this recent example of an iteration:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/480892248086a40f0e4ee5610b5bcee0.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Made in August 2022
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8fd1a2ed542c39db5205c6430fd692ba.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The nuance of these images are completely different but the core message is the same: address problems as they form to avoid it getting so convoluted that they become difficult to manage.

For me, one of the best parts of thinking in visual metaphors is the forcing function of having to get crystal clear on what you’re trying to say in your content.

\textbf{CLARITY = iteration x time}

Ultimately, whether version 2 is better or worse is irrelevant. The act of creating a different articulation opens another door to how deeply you think about the idea.

When you’re ready and if you’re curious to learn how to make visual metaphors like I do, \textbf{sign up for the waitlist for the next Thinking in Visual Metaphors cohort. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What most people get wrong about iteration and change}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-02-13}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/cd3d14fe5694642597e94e75c3e06510.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This Japanese concept is the secret to staying consistent in your pursuits:

\textbf{Ikigai} (生き甲斐)\\
⦿ \textit{iki} - means to live\\
⦿ \textit{gai} - means value or worth (literally translated to "beautiful shell")

Ikigai roughly means your "reason for being"--your purpose.

Find your purpose and you find the foundation to build your dream.

If you’re interested in learning more, I’d recommend checking out \textbf{“Ikigai: The Japanese Secret to a Long and Happy Life” by Héctor García. }

It took me a while to align what I do online and what I do in my day job as a teacher, but I finally found the words to articulate my ikigai:

\textbf{Encourage people to live a more creative life to make the world a more creative place. }

What's your ikigai?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-02-13}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why you accomplish less than you want...but more than you think}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-02-27}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/c8a27074c4860aa285ee2545018821e1.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
An unfortunate truth:\\
\textbf{Good judgment comes from experience.}\\
\textbf{Experience comes from bad judgment.}

I used to write this in on the first page of each journal I would gift to my filmmaking students.

\textbf{The biggest lessons are a result of making an expensive mistake} (expensive in time, money…heartbreak).

The earlier in our lives we make these mistakes, the more time we have to enjoy the compounding benefits of the lessons they teach.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b6546c7157e28e749231e098a49bcad7.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{What people "miss" about success.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why you accomplish less than you want...but more than you think}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-02-27}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A simple trick to elevate the impact of a bar graph: \\
\textbf{Substitute the bars in the graph with a symbol. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/45ec8553203d0b9d00bb824e2d917fcb.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Version 1
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f8d2d5bb1e2895700c7a713743ab5558.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
In version 1, I clarified this idea I had about how deeply you have to understand something to teach it. It got the message across but one of my core creative practices is to \textbf{keep pushing}.

How can I make this: \\
• clearer?\\
• more insightful? \\
• more memorable?

That’s when I came up with version 2 to add another layer of nuance to the visual: substitute the bars with books.

This technique comes from my filmmaking background and I call it: \textbf{superimposition}. It’s one of the tools I teach in my \textbf{Thinking in Visual Metaphors} course.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why you accomplish less than you want...but more than you think}

If you think others have it figured out while you're still struggling, remember this:

\textbf{The Swan Paradox:}\\
It takes an obscene amount of effort to make what you're doing look effortless.

And the key thing to remember is to stay afloat, the effort's ongoing.\\
It's what it means to be consistent.

You'll drown if you rely only on burst efforts.

Pace yourself.
\end{minipage}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Japanese philosophy that got me over perfectionism}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-03-12}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This idea is at the core of my creative philosophy…and it might help if you struggle with perfectionism as much as I do:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/fb443804a8195eceef0f096d2c4c3f99.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Quote from Ernest Heminway, “A Farewell To Arms”

\textbf{Wabi-Sabi}…

…a Zen aesthetic ideal that celebrates flaws, recognizing the beauty in imperfection and incompleteness.

The practice of wabi-sabi is the perfect (🥁) counternote to perfectionism.

You’ll find this philosophy practiced in the Japanese artform, \textbf{kintsugi}.

In kintsugi, pottery is intentionally broken, then repaired with a golden lacquer to highlight its damage.

One thing I’ve learned from 20 years of teaching and making 400+ visual metaphors is that art isn’t about being accurate. It’s about being interesting.

And what makes you interesting is your unique combination of imperfections and flaws.

Instead of trying to airbrush them away, highlight them.

Your imperfections are the feature, not the bug.

When you’re ready, consider checking out \textbf{Thinking in Visual Metaphors}. Registration for Cohort 4 closes in less than 2 weeks.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e9f5cefec10bcfaed5660eaf3c9f0d6f.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Learn how to make AI work for you.}

AI won’t take your job, but a person using AI might. That’s why 500,000+ professionals read The Rundown – the free newsletter that keeps you updated on the latest AI news and teaches you how to apply it in just 5 minutes a day.

Subscribe with one click.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The question most people don't ask me and why it matters}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-03-26}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/51ec5c2a1471533e53ea27a556dbf422.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Comfort zones are tiny prisons that keep us }\\
\textbf{from experiencing the vastness of life.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The question most people don't ask me and why it matters}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-03-26}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I get asked all the time what software* I use to make my visuals.

I understand why it’s asked but this question frames the wrong problem.

Software enables thinking, but without the thinking, a piece of software is just an empty shell.

The more important question to ask is: \\
how do you translate an idea into a visual metaphor?

For me, it’s a 3-step process.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/17c5ff7d616dd93bd357fc9f7f5419cd.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Everything is downstream of clarity. Without it, no amount of graphics will resonate with the audience.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/bdd08457ad1465c80eb3125f4af5d13a.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
You need to give your message shape so your audience can process it fast and easily.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/4b8caf9e9763bd0019d0f9866b047eb8.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This step is critical. Most visual thinkers believe you have to blatantly hammer your reader over the head with the message. But this makes the reader passive.

I believe in trusting the reader.

Leave space in the message for the audience to fill in the gap themselves. It’s not about you looking smart. It’s about making your reader feel smart.

We’re just touching the surface here, but this is the general overview of the process: \textbf{Clarify =\textgreater{} Simplify =\textgreater{} Amplify}

*For the record, the software I use is Procreate on the iPad with an Apple Pencil. 😊

P.S. If you want to start translating your own ideas into visuals, it’s not too late to sign up for \textbf{Cohort 4 of Thinking in Visual Metaphors}\textbf{ }but time’s running out for enrollment. Class begins Wednesday, March 27th!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-03-26}

\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{3 best returns on investments 👆}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The question most people don't ask me and why it matters}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-03-26}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a3ed29c2bd9b16daeec93ee4276a0976.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{A friendly reminder to appreciate the effort it takes }\\
\textbf{to make something look effortless. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Where to focus your attention to improve your quality of life}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-04-09}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
If you’ve followed me for a while, you might notice I’ll often revisit an idea—to find a different articulation of that message.

There’re 3 reasons why:

Each articulation forces diving into \textbf{deeper understanding}.

\textbf{Improves pattern recognition} of how things are connected.

Different metaphors will \textbf{impact people differently}.

There’s also a more personal reason worth mentioning—it keeps my perfectionist monster at bay.

If I know the visual I’m creating is just ‘one of many,’ then I’m less precious about finding the ‘perfect analogy.’

Here’s an example of a recent articulation of “fancy language vs simple language.”
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/63378dafd8099973767c6dd5237dd4a8.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
And here are two earlier articulations of that same idea:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/396d389c48dc7bb797a3d26fa9c01ab2.png}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Where to focus your attention to improve your quality of life}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-04-09}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/7a19899502a84c63a7d2ae0fd0394e56.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The role of a teacher. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Where to focus your attention to improve your quality of life}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-04-09}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/35d3deee1d8e4992f40e5e397938f2fd.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
"The master has failed more times than the beginner has even tried."

Most people compare destinations without comparing journeys.

I'll give you an example…

For 13 years, Mike Winkelmann (aka "beeple") made a piece of art, everyday (aptly called his “everydays”).

Day 5,000, Mike takes each of his everydays and stitches them together into an NFT of a mosaic called: "The First 5000 Days."

And...

October 2021, this NFT sells for…wait for it—\\
\$69 million.

Media labeled it an "overnight success."

But there's no such thing as an overnight success. Only over time success.

13 years of shooting daily shots.

Beeple still creates today. 6183 days and counting!

This is what it means to be a master.

Hit or miss, you keep shooting.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why focusing on one thing at a time is a superpower}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-04-25}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/1173a0db1c267ca1d61b6f0d13c9b4d2.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
“You can do anything, but not everything.” (…all at once)

I admit, before I started posting online a couple years ago, I was notoriously bad at this. And my wife argues I still have quite the room to grow in other domains (like tidying up the bedroom!).

But I make conscious (and often painful) efforts to focus on one cup at a time when it comes to being a creator.

Add your \textbf{“ONE thing you're prioritizing this week” to the conversation here. }

My priority this week is to reflect on my father’s life through journaling.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why focusing on one thing at a time is a superpower}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-04-25}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A question came up in my \textbf{Thinking in Visual Metaphors} course about \textbf{avatars}.

Do you create a reference sheet for your avatar with different moods and poses?

This isn’t a bad idea, but I don’t recommend spending the time to do this when you’re first starting out.

Why?

For years, I struggled to make anything because I thought I needed to do x, y, and z to START. Turned out it was just productive procrastination.

It wasn’t until I realized, you know what? It’s totally fine to build as you go…make what you need as you need it (applies to many things, not just visuals).

An hour spent making 20 different facial expressions is an hour not spent on creating the visual that needs only 2. And once you have those 2, you can reuse them like this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/11e30b310e17184ed0f28b0d384f7fb9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ceb9a65f3b0673eb60cb464a6e36f474.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The 80/20 rule applies here: You’ll probably use 20\% of those poses for 80\% of your visuals.

So build that reference sheet, but only as you’re building your visuals.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ca498544e646fb882398d1e0034e12e5.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Build as you go is my philosophy.

P.S. If you’re ready to start \textbf{Thinking in Visual Metaphors}, the next cohort starts late May.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why focusing on one thing at a time is a superpower}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-04-25}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/12a9f6ed36bc29cc7bb5fa7c88c04483.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The longest journey you'll ever make.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why focusing on one thing at a time is a superpower}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-04-25}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/cbd04756ee263ef493152c95148bd741.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Most of us (myself included 😅) get caught up in shiny object syndrome which splinters our focus a mile wide, but an inch deep.

It’s the paradox of the creator. We seek novelty through experimentation, but need to improve what we do through repetition.

If we truly want to upgrade our thinking and skillsets, we need to dive an inch wide, a mile deep.

The shiny objects will always be waiting for us at the surface when we come back up.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What most people get wrong about how to stand out as a creator}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-05-14}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b143a59387b055a4c003e87200a60d48.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Friendly reminder: Perfection shouldn’t even be the goal. }

This is at the heart of my creator philosophy:

One perfect circle looks just like any other perfect circle. Most people think they can’t draw because they’re comparing their drawings to what they believe it SHOULD look like.

But if you want to make stuff that stands out, it’s less important to be accurate and more important to be interesting.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What most people get wrong about how to stand out as a creator}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-05-14}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I’ve been teaching film \& animation for 20 years, and I try to bring filmmaking concepts into my visuals whenever I can. One of my favorite things to play with is \textbf{movement! }

Now how do we add movement to a static image? \\
\textbf{Motion Lines. }

There are 3 main types:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/10351bae12fbf3ca9801464bdb323c5f.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Try it yourself! Here’s a simple exercise to make straight motion:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a5b2ac22a98d07d49ee2819371e604f3.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Draw a simple circle
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/07128bf0fadd1c067fc77d361f55fe53.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
And make some straight lines over it!

It’s as simple as that!

And by the way, if you’re keen to learn how to make visual metaphors, enrollment for Thinking in Visual Metaphors is open for another week! 28 students have already enrolled in Cohort 5!
\end{minipage}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What most people get wrong about how to stand out as a creator}

\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a63a99c60eb0ddf4b9ba25859ff33661.png}

\textbf{The price of admission for success.}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to overcome your impossible standards}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-05-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/503f6b35b967b6ae47a9c1f99a5367e3.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Avoid the second mistake.}\\
Inspired by James Clear’s book, \textbf{Atomic Habits}.

Now the trick is how?

The best piece of advice I’ve heard from James Clear is, “reduce the scope to maintain the habit.”

Most of my life I’ve held almost impossible to meet standards, for myself and others. While this was useful to me for a season, I realized over time those standards distorted my creative output into an all or nothing approach.

The harsh truth is that \textbf{a balanced life doesn’t mean balanced days.} Balance comes in the form of an averaging of your days.

There will be days when I only get a few push-ups or a brisk walk in for exercise. There are days when I get home so late that I only have enough time with the kids for a short cuddle and bedtime story.

The point is to embrace the imperfect messiness of it all. Miss a day, you’re human. Try your best to get back on the bike day 2, even if it means you don’t go as far forward as you’d like.

A little progress is still progress.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to overcome your impossible standards}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-05-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I have a simple hack to fight my perfectionist tendencies:

\textbf{Draw on paper…with a pen.}

This practice forces you to:

Stop being precious

Be more efficient with your lines

Avoid wasting time erasing to make things perfect
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
%\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ef1ea0d4c3e11ddb083690f8403143b8.gif}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to overcome your impossible standards}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-05-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a805c243f8b393c74310115be856084e.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Friendly reminder of the day.}

I try to think of my visual metaphors as “friendly reminders” to the reader (and myself). I hope they FEEL true, like a familiar echo…that somehow got lost in the sea of relentless noise.

This one is a simple reminder to myself that the negative stuff we each face day in and day out are what help us appreciate the positive stuff.

If you like friendly reminders, I posted a bunch more\textbf{ to start the week here. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to overcome your impossible standards}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-05-29}

\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}

\textbf{Perception vs reality of routines}

I used to hate routines. But nothing gets you to love routines faster than having kids. 😆

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What learning the guitar taught me about progress}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-06-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e4cdf7e00d13e62329d9b688265dc5a4.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Most progress is invisible until it's not.

When I first learned to play the guitar—

E-chord? No problem. \\
C-chord? No problem. \\
But then I got to the G-chord, and I was like, what the hell is this?!

I thought, "how in the world do fingers make this shape?"

Day to day, I tried to play that freaking G-chord.

But no sound. All I felt was the pain of metal strings carving into my fingers. I couldn't see progress but for some reason I trusted the process.

And eventually one day out of no where, I heard \textit{strum}...\\
the sweet release of that G-chord! 🫠

That was the first time in my life I had proof that just because you can't see progress doesn't mean you're not making progress.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What learning the guitar taught me about progress}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-06-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3b92ec2c227d466815fbca1a7ffabad1.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{A critical shift in thinking to make for leaders. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What learning the guitar taught me about progress}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-06-18}

{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ecf16e85deb3bf9c9e27c714dfc09374.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{It's in your own hands.}

\textbf{Life is short. }
\end{minipage}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3e4fee0486287afc4ec882cb8411c3d5.png}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Visual IDEAs: Why making daily visuals is a superpower}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-08-06}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/5ae69c5bc648b9f5cd740f5e0080bb94.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{It gets messier before it doesn't. }

One of the most beneficial aspects of writing is that it gives your memory and thinking structure. Random events and emotions can be organized with a beginning, middle and end.

But often, I find myself creating more chaos in the process before finding the thread to tie everything together.

Ah but the satisfaction and clarity once that baggage you’ve been carrying is organized feels oh so good! 😁

“This is the only real concern of the artist, \\
to recreate out of the disorder of life \\
that order which is art.”
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Visual IDEAs: Why making daily visuals is a superpower}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-08-06}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The beauty of creating visuals daily is the ability to \textbf{repurpose} the assets you build over time.

For example:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/755767468ae14c102ee8154d60a9e02f.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This is the 21st visual I ever made (very different than today I know 😅)
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/cdfb206b7fab4ea04315384ede477878.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Here’s that same firefly repurposed a year later!

This is a superpower because the more you create, the more you CAN create!

For example, this \textbf{recent carousel on the difference between amateurs vs professionals}\textbf{*} that went viral were mostly visuals I gave new life by repurposing them.

This means even though in the beginning you’re doing a lot of heavy lifting, the more reps you do, the bigger you grow your personal library of assets. And that means you don’t always have to start from scratch!

P.S. If you’re ready to start building your own visual library, you may want to join the next cohort of \textbf{Thinking in Visual Metaphors} in September. Be sure to sign up for the waitlist to be one of the first to know when registration starts!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/11e7b17799d0c82d0c1d0f04b2b1860e.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
*I should note to be an amateur is a beautiful thing. “Amateur” comes from the Latin word for lover (amator). I’m a proud amateur guitarist! 😬 The problem comes \textit{if I want to become a pro} guitarist. Pursuing it as a career forces changes in my mindset that need to happen if I want to avoid disappointment.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Visual IDEAs: Why making daily visuals is a superpower}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-08-06}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d10b157208e23ee754caa35794bf3965.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The Swan Paradox: }\\
It takes an obscene amount of effort to make what you're doing look effortless.\\
To stay afloat, the effort never stops.

This is what it means to be "consistent."

But be careful. You'll drown if you only rely on burst efforts. \\
Pace yourself.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Visual IDEAs: Why making daily visuals is a superpower}

\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Definition of failure. }

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to find happiness where you are}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-08-20}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/c272761b4b39b14bc97b6e36580a9cbe.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The one word never to include in an apology.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to find happiness where you are}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-08-20}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I’m currently reading \textbf{Dr. Peter Attia’s book, Outlive}, which is a very thorough and detailed book summarizing most of Dr. Attia’s best practices.

The one thing I noticed reading the book though is that its jargon filled and could probably benefit from some visual thinking to cement the messages.

The example below is a chart Dr. Attia fought tooth and nail to put into the book but was overruled by his editors. Now I don’t know about you, but I can see why. I had to listen to the explanation twice and then spend another few minutes really looking over this chart to get the point.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/34dfbfbf68ffcffd6e56a4a8ba7d96c8.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Today’s quick lesson if you are trying to convey a message in a visual:\\
\textbf{Stop presenting data. Instead, present the point of the data. }

For example, here’s ONE of the interpretations of the data (there are many other helpful interpretations that EACH deserve their own visual):
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/206b9417657fc1bf2309b48d062be4ce.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Based on Dr. Peter Attia’s Data

It’s true we lose some nuance from simplifying, but we also save our reader from spending as much time as I did to interpret the data.

You can always complement the visual with the hardcore data in an appendix (or if giving a live-presentation, a QR code to a website with the charts)

P.S. If you want to go deeper to learn how to create visual metaphors, \textbf{click here to sign up for the waitlist. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to find happiness where you are}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-08-20}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3f66053afd01580c3f08eac02a873fed.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The pursuit of having what you want vs wanting what you have.}

It’s all too easy to miss all the things you have right where you are.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to find happiness where you are}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-08-20}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d3b0b6c5904017573a85006d404c3019.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{The distance between your dreams and reality is not as far as you think.}

I overplan. Overanalyze. Overthink most things. It may be why my \textbf{overthinking visual carousel }struck a chord with so many folks a couple weeks ago.

Before I made my first online post, I kept thinking I had to figure everything out before starting.

Questions like:

What's my niche?

Who am I to talk about this?

And hasn't everything that needs to be said about everything already been said?!

So I kept thinking...and waiting...for over 10+ years!

The biggest lesson I learned after starting was you can't steer a parked car (as the saying goes).

99\% of that analysis paralysis was just in my head.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why you should embrace FOMO}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-09-17}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A quick tip to simplify a metaphor:\\
Play with the \textbf{AMOUNT} of an element in the visual.

It’s a helpful way to frame an idea so its meaning is more easily understood by the reader.

To start, try this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/bb9c3411777c15a7bf4ff67806015ccb.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Multiply the quantity of the object…
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f46edc8abf8f86f01ae85681802fc6a5.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
…or scale its size.

P.S. When you’re ready to start creating your own visuals, \textbf{sign up for the next cohort of Thinking in Visual Metaphors ↗} .
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

Back to the drawing board! 😆

Recently, I shared a first animation of one of my visual metaphors. There’s plenty of room to grow and experiment in this space, but it did make me reflect…what is lost and what is gained in the reader’s experience when we add motion?

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Are you reaching your full potential?}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-10-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/91895fea85321b431cb13b85407009c7.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Motion = staying busy }\\
\textbf{Action = focused execution}

I used to wear “being busy” as a badge of honor. But a lesson I’m relearning is doing a lot and doing what matters are not the same thing.

What’s worse is the busier I get, the less I focus on the latter.

Don’t make this same mistake. Create space for a few moments today to think about how you might position this week to take action on the things that matter most.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The problem with low-hanging fruit}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-11-26}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/ba7397c58347b3031304748f055dc731.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A mistake a lot of folks make:

Falling into "the collector's fallacy" trap--\\
Believing that by collecting more information, we somehow absorb it to grow.

It feels productive to:

highlight more books

bookmark more articles

listen to more podcasts

“If more information was the answer, then we'd all be billionaires with perfect abs.”

Real progress happens through decisions, action and commitment.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The problem with low-hanging fruit}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-11-26}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b00a1548d330ba327803eb0a29582711.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
“If we only do what we’re familiar with, we might miss what we’ve been made for.”
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The problem with low-hanging fruit}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-11-26}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b895e36605db1947861ca587163275b7.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Friendly reminder:} Always check you’re climbing the right mountain.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Building a creative habit in 2025}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2024-12-10}

\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/1f461a4e51b14ffcdfe9a0f758ff9b37.png}

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
One of my favorite idea learned this year from Adam Grant: \\
the word "\textbf{sonder"} from the \textbf{Dictionary of Obscure Sorrows by John Koenig}

Some of my other favorites from the dictionary:

\textbf{HARMONIA}\\
n.an itchy sense of dread when life feels just a hint too peaceful—when everyone seems to get along suspiciously well, with an eerie stillness that makes you want to brace for the inevitable collapse, or burn it down yourself.\\
(I feel like I’m in an unhealthy constant state of harmonia. Am I the only one? 🤔)

\textbf{ANCHORAGE}\\
n.the desire to hold on to time as it passes, like trying to keep your grip on a rock in the middle of a river, feeling the weight of the current against your chest while your elders float on downstream, calling over the roar of the rapids, “Just let go—it’s okay—let go.”
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{There's a reason why dough must rest before it can rise.}

This is something I'm still working on.

Resting may seem commonsensical, but when you've built habits around rolling forward at full momentum, it can be tough slowing down.

Earlier this year, I scheduled a weekend to relax, but I was shocked how little I could shut off without feeling guilty or anxious I should be doing more. It wasn't until last month when I got sick I realized there's only so far you can go if you don't learn to rest.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

The most interesting thing about a fixed vs growth mindset is where and how it's applied.

\textbf{Example:} We can be growth minded about getting good at basketball, but fixed in our math ability. We each have self-belief blind spots where we see things as fixed.

The good news is self-awareness of these spots is a useful first step to getting closer to where we want to be.

\small
There is no one-size fits all formula for work-life balance.

It’s personal to you. A moving target based on the stage of your life.

Arrange and rearrange the pieces until you feel aligned.

And remember, you may need to reshape the balance as you shift from one stage of life to another.

What felt right in your 20s will most likely not fit where you are in your 40s.
\end{minipage}

only light can do that. \\

only love can do that.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why friendships are like trees}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-02-04}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/98df2aa56d3f8b94498c3482c54b2c25.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
There's beauty in having all 3 friendships in our lives, because they each serve a different purpose. But the most distress I’ve felt in my personal friendships is confusing one for another so it’s helpful to know which friends are which.

Leaves flow in and out of our lives as new leaves fill their place (this is natural so we shouldn’t be too sad when it happens).

Branches—we see daily. Some are stronger than others. They can endure pressure, but only so much before breaking.

Root friends keep us grounded. Often unseen, but we feel their impact and stability.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How money is like water}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-02-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/7a84f76ff0797606697143505a271415.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I wish I knew this in my 20s:

There'll never be a perfect someday.\\
But there's always an imperfect now.

So how do you start?

With these 3 simple words: \textbf{“I am doing.”}

Not “I will…” (procrastinating)

Not “I should’ve…” (regret)

But \textbf{“I am…”} (right here, right now)
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How money is like water}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-02-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3bbe5f2db63cd88de2db77695b545f27.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
This is the biggest regret most "successful people" have.

The reason is simple:

Money is a means to an end (not the end itself).

But often in the pursuit of more, we sacrifice the very things money was supposed to help solve (or at least make easier).

When the bucket is full, nourish your flowers.

Inspired by Sahil Bloom's book, \textbf{"The 5 Types of Wealth”}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/35b8bd78f61272ff40df6dfe9596afc2.jpg}

\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}

People really seemed to like this behind-the-scenes first draft on LinkedIn so sharing it here 😊
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How risks are like being stranded on a boat}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-03-04}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f8f9c706d866a024de7c3835900403c0.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Change is risky, but so is standing still.

Most of my career, my whole identity was “Mr. Milani”—\\
A high school film \& animation teacher.

Now I love being a teacher. But whenever students asked, “What are you making?” I froze. Teaching creativity, yet creating nothing of my own, left me feeling like an imposter.

And then the pandemic hit—and confronted me with a scary question: If I can’t teach, then who am I?

One night as I journaled about my need to start creating, I had déjà-vu. So I flipped through old notebooks and found the same words—written 11 years ago!

“I need to at least start.” (\textit{oof})

It seems when you stand in a leaky boat long enough, you stop noticing the water.

So doubts and all, I took a leap—and, yes, I stumbled right into the sharks. 😂\\
(No one gets it right the first try)

The lesson: when you procrastinate a decision, you’re still making a choice to stay where you are.

If you’ve been wanting to make a change, maybe it’s time to test the waters.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How risks are like being stranded on a boat}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-03-04}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/30ef4489e43e23f20f928aeac4749334.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
↳ The simplest hack to overcome “disappointments of outcome” when you post online.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How risks are like being stranded on a boat}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-03-04}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/69482c3f6fc9958f4b2d0ce90322dfc8.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Friendly reminder: You can't fill every cup (and that's perfectly okay).

Work demands your focus

Your partner needs quality 1-on-1 time

Family deserves your presence

Friends want you to show up when it matters

The more cups you try to fill:\\
↳ Faster yours runs empty\\
↳ Longer it takes to fill back up.

You can’t give 100\% to everyone, every day. There's always a trade-off.

You can have it all. Just not all at once.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to look at your fears differently}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-03-19}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/fbad289beb295f0a312569c0d1373ed9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Fear is a mile wide, an inch deep.

You stand at the edge, convincing yourself the water’s too deep.\\
You take a step, but you don’t sink! Your foot hits solid ground.\\
You question why you doubted yourself for so long.

You change—action always clears the mud in your head.\\
You remember fear grows in hesitation, shrinks in motion.\\
You move forward—realizing the gap was all in your mind.

Inaction magnifies self-doubt → Action shrinks it
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to look at your fears differently}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-03-19}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The most common reason people don’t create visual metaphors is the limiting belief they “can’t draw.” But visual metaphors isn’t about “making things pretty,” it’s about making things pithy.

Today’s bite-sized lesson is how we can communicate big ideas with simple shapes and arrows!

I’ll keep it short \& sweet with 3 examples:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d72867433cfdeda67359d0a996924458.png}

\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
There’s no doubt people are more attracted to pretty things. But the good news is you don’t have to be Leonardo da Vinci to make images that get readers to think.

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why failing is not what you think}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-03}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/6ae425b8fef49eb0b14dc832e2365d1d.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
There are two ladders in your career.

But remember, what helped you climb the first ladder may not be useful in the second.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why failing is not what you think}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-03}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Engaging in creativity is like building a LEGO set without instructions.

With each new piece, the whole thing warps and twists. You have a vague sense of the shape, but there inevitably is a point where key pieces go missing and you have no idea how to move forward.

The lights turn off and you start running into brick walls that come out of nowhere. This dark void is called \textbf{“The Zone of Ambiguity,”} a temporary but necessary space.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/311e497de466902e4e9348ada58d6317.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The only difference between someone who considers themselves creative and someone who doesn’t is the confidence that the \textbf{Zone of Ambiguity is a temporary space.}

And you build confidence through seeing you can in fact can find your way through. With each rep, that gap between ambiguity and insight shrinks smaller, but it will always exist.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why failing is not what you think}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-03}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/5b0457238efda097a778010386e24cf5.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f9fc9817ea037aa75beaf30b04f56495.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I used to have this T-shirt I loved in high school from a brand called "No Fear."

On the back it said, "There's nothing in life more painful than regret."

Everything we want has a sacrifice.

Everything we don't want has a consequence.

But one thing’s for sure—the regret of "what could've been" is often heavier than the discipline it takes to change the present.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why failing is not what you think}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-03}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/9c770471a730d7645834fd63545c5201.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
To be clear, no one enjoys failing.\\
It sucks to feel like you're not good at something.

But there'll always be learning pains. Accept the miss and adjust your aim.

Don't quit before you've given yourself a chance to feel what it's like to get good.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The Myth of Doing It All}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/9d206d03120e55f40c584d1dc761400d.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Let’s be real. It’s HARD to prioritize.

If you’ve followed me for a while, this visual metaphor may feel familiar. That’s because it’s not the first time I’ve articulated this idea. \textbf{(check out this one if you’re curious)}

The thing is most people (myself included) want to do everything all at once. But that’s a surefire recipe for feeling overwhelmed and frustrated at a lack of making real progress on any one thing.

The thing no one tells when you’ve got multiple irons in the fire is you’re probably going to get burned (out).

And as difficult as it is, one thing at a time is a far more useful approach to truly build momentum.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How Progress Is Like Crossing a River}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/853dd73c23018493a8347834ab4ec27e.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Most people let fear stop them before they start.

"What if I fail?"\\
"What if people judge me?"\\
"What if I'm not good enough?"

These questions paralyze us.\\
Try flipping the script.

Replace "what if" with "EVEN IF."\\
"Even if I fail, I'll learn something valuable."\\
"Even if people judge me, I'll grow stronger."\\
"Even if I'm not perfect, I'll be better than yesterday."

The most successful people I know aren't fearless.\\
They simply move forward, "even if" scared.

\textbf{Read the full post here.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How Progress Is Like Crossing a River}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A quick and easy visual metaphor anyone can make ↴
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b8098475b98eacf77cfe5cd2e20796e6.jpeg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A useful way to show the Pareto Principle (80/20 Rule). You can use this for anything where you want to highlight the importance of the smaller element—like the handful of customers who drive most of your revenue.

The big square is the majority (80\%), while that small detached piece represents the minority (20\%).

Know what else can show a majority/minority relationship? That’s right! A pie chart! So you can think of this framework as a variation of the pie chart but with just a different texture.

What I love about this metaphor is its instant clarity. That small piece calls out, “I’m small, but mighty!”

P.S. When you’re ready to learn more frameworks like this, you can \textbf{secure your spot for Thinking in Visual Metaphors. }Enrollment for Cohort 11 launches today!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-04-29}

\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d815d5a039c3e11b81514146a5180a40.png}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why low-hanging fruit are dangerous}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-05-12}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I had an embarrassing near-miss last week that taught me 3 valuable lessons about visual metaphors.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/b0d773baa1da05ead9bc13a317251618.png}

\begin{center}

\end{minipage}

\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why low-hanging fruit are dangerous}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-05-12}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/d21e78993183bbdea6c971654ab56a64.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I've been rethinking leadership lately.

Your impact isn't measured by how high you climb.\\
It's counted in how many others climbed BECAUSE of you.

\textbf{"Top-of-the-ladder" folks:}\\
→ Measure success by title and status\\
→ Chase personal achievements\\
→ Stand alone at the summit

\textbf{True leaders:}\\
→ Carve out paths for their teams\\
→ Often work quietly at ground level\\
→ Find delight in other people's wins
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why low-hanging fruit are dangerous}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-05-12}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/291c9a31016921fba39b052ace8aed0b.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Day 1 is all about courage.\\
Day 30 is proof of your commitment.

You'll be surprised what you can do in a month if you show up daily.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The time-saving power of one simple word}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-05-27}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3929fbe3c58b67d704cf1901204a3bd6.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Success isn’t about being a genius on your first shot. Just ask the data (which tells a sobering story).

1st time startup founders success rate: 18\%

Those same founders success rate by 10th attempt: 65\%

"Better than yesterday" isn't just motivational fluff. The idea of becoming an overnight success is a fantasy. A harmful one. (and this doesn’t just relate to entrepreneurship) It's how mastery actually works.

Think about it. If you improve just 1\% daily, you'll be 37x better in one year.\\
Not 365\% better. \\
3,700\% better.

You might ask, how do you actually improve 1\% daily?

Answer 3 simple questions:

“What went slightly better today than yesterday?"

“What small improvement can I make tomorrow?"

“Where am I aiming my next arrow?”

It’s not about having perfect aim. \\
It’s not about being the best.\\
It’s just being a little better. Everyday.

P.S. I talk more about the importance of consistency in \textbf{this post. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The time-saving power of one simple word}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-05-27}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
If you’re a long time reader, you may have noticed I iterated a new banner!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/0a40c1527e22a739c91d866e9203b7f9.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Iterations!

Settled on version 10 if you're counting! 😅

Here's the funny thing about iteration. You need fresh eyes to see straight.

That's why finding your creative safety net matters. Those trusted few who'll tell you:

"This font feels off"

"Actually, the shadow is too far too the right"

"The old logo had more charm because…"

Without them, you're just rearranging pixels in the dark. Find your people.\\
(shoutout to Hannah Wilson and Michael J Boorman — Hype crew for life!)
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/cc7318039901da5fddcd7dbc56a012ae.png}

Time doesn’t disappear.\\

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why friendships get harder as we get older}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-06-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/0907b065c4e0efa5e6c457af7e90c957.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
As kids, friendships were easy.\\
Same classes. Same recess. Same milestones.

As adults, friendships are complicated.\\
Because we’re all running different races at difference paces.

Getting married. Getting divorced. \\
Starting over. Settling down.\\
Having kids. Choosing not to.

I used to think growing apart meant growing away from each other.\\
Now I understand it just means growing in different directions.

At different speeds. Toward different things.

"I'm here" doesn't mean "I'm stuck"\\
"You're there" doesn't mean "You've left me"\\
It just means we're all finding our way.

But somehow...still sending memes at 2am like nothing's changed. 😄
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

The thing about circles is...You don't always know you're in one.

You row hard, make waves.\\
Staying in motion, but repeating the same patterns.

Testing if you’re in a circle is simple:\\
When did you last feel uncomfortable?

Because comfort and growth rarely share the same boat.\\
Maybe today's the day to point somewhere new.

Even if you have to row alone for a bit.
\end{minipage}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why I'm not worried about AI Images}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-07-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}

\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
When you use other people's definition of success to measure your happiness, consider this:

You wouldn't use other people's house key to open your front door.\\
So why use their scorecard to measure your life?

Their success might be a corner office.Yours might be Tuesday afternoons free.\\
Their win might be scaling to seven figures.\\
Yours might be to make it to all your son's soccer games.

Both are valid.

But happiness has never been a one-size fits all game. It's a personal fit.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why I'm not worried about AI Images}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-07-15}

{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]

\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
If ALL you use is AI images to communicate your ideas, you are slowly blending in. There’s a place for it in your process, but how do you differentiate yourself from everyone else using AI?

My hypothesis: People will get bored of AI images (if not already). And that means there’s still opportunity. Remember: how you draw something is unique to you, imperfections and all. And it’s those very human imperfections you might fear that make your work interesting.

If you choose to lean into it, it may turn into your competitive advantage to stand out over the AI slop that is shaping the creator landscape today.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why showing up doesn't mean showing up perfectly.}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-10-21}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/5a8f83625005abd39c142ad9d7581ab4.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
If you’ve been subscribed for a while, you may have noticed I’ve not sent out a newsletter in over a month. That miss has been gnawing away at me daily. A lot of it has come from setting priorities around health and family (see my last email). But if I’m honest, more of it comes from breaking the streak built over several years.

What’s funny when you aim for a goal is that the misses often teach far more than the bullseye. And my recent misses on the newsletter have retaught me the importance of consistency and more importantly momentum.

Showing up doesn’t mean showing up perfectly.

Some days will splash. Some days will drip.\\
Both water the garden.

What garden are you watering as we head into the holidays? Hit reply. I’d love to know!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{There's a difference between what's cool and what's meaningful}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-11-19}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/77f4c4e5ba3f20cf77ec363b86f1c0a8.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
We become what we refuse to release.

I had a friend who used to collect scars like they were stamps. As if he was curating a museum of hurts and betrayals.

Don’t get me wrong. He was justified.

But over time, it distorted into a weird paradox.\\
Holding the pain validated his story.\\
But the pain then became the story.

The thing is pain can be a teacher. But it’s meant to visit, not move in. And you can acknowledge the hurt without making it your home.

It’s possible the things we can’t release have already released us. We're just the last to know.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

Teaching others teaches yourself.
