\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Are you preparing or are you procrastinating?}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-02}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/5431ee9fbea77dc4a542e3a10ce66182.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Not what you think about. Not what you plan to do. What you actually practice daily.

It becomes non-negotiable when it's tied to who you are.

\textbf{Writers write }(even when it's hard).

\textbf{Athletes train} (even when they're tired).

\textbf{Leaders lead} (even when they doubt).

We act in alignment with who we believe we are.\\
\textbf{Belief → Practice → Identity}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Are you preparing or are you procrastinating?}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-02}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/9268573813fbc0360e983058ed92bfc9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
When I turned 40, I read over two dozen books on writing and creativity.\\
Guess how many words I wrote that same year. Zero.

Books are maps, not the journey.\\
Starting points, not destinations.\\
Don't build a library where you should build experience.

It wasn’t until I committed to post online daily that I built any forward momentum.

Read one good book. Apply something fully. Then maybe read another.

\textbf{Productive:} "Let me understand the basics to start”\\
\textbf{Productive procrastination: }"Let me understand everything"

At some point, you have to close the book to open the door.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What’s the difference between generosity and strategy?}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-16}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/bde5ff3ab4b31b99fa416e12b8dcf556.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
What’s the difference between generosity and strategy?

Or more precisely, what connects your actions and your expectations? (whether it’s spoken aloud or a silent understanding)

“I’ll help you ONLY WHEN you help me" → Transactional

"I'll help you BECAUSE you helped me" → Reciprocal

"I'll help you SO THAT you'll help me later" → Manipulative

"I'll help you." → Unconditional

Some relationships are meant to be transactional. That's okay. It’s how most of the world works. In fact, many of our closest and longstanding relationships fall into the reciprocal (there’s nothing wrong with that).

But the relationships that hit different are the ones that don’t keep score. \\
And it's worth knowing which kind you're in and which kind you're offering.

So here's my question for you this week: When was a time you wanted to be unconditional but then found yourself transition into one of these other modes? (or vice versa)

Reply and let me know. While I can't answer every email, I read every single response!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What’s the difference between generosity and strategy?}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-16}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The best visual metaphors reveal an insight that \textbf{feels new, but still oddly familiar. }They remind us of something we quietly know in our mind, heart, or soul, but due to the frantic hustle \& bustle of the day to day, we forget!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/45f3c04dbcf151c6bdd7a225e2fa9cc0.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The key is using what’s familiar to act as the relational bridge between what we know and what feels foreign. Usually the bridge connects (or corrects) a behavior or belief.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8e9040af525f88582daecec111a347a2.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
For example, if you’re struggling to find pockets of happiness in your life and I just said “fix your environment and you might be a little happier,” it doesn’t feel very insightful.

So instead, I start with an assumption of what you might familiar (and it’s helpful to point out no assumption holds true for everyone). But what if I assumed you might know what it feels like to chase a butterfly?
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What’s the difference between generosity and strategy?}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-16}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/047fd6cae26c23a618a71f8655269153.png}

\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{What’s the difference between generosity and strategy?}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-16}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/24a49f03ec3f80760a43b3eab8507af6.png}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to use evidence to build confidence}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-30}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e83c09ee515f52266cffce3137af6ee0.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
For years, runners believed the human body couldn't run a mile in under four minutes. Doctors said it was physically impossible!

Then on May 6, 1954, British runner Roger Bannister ran it in 3:59.4.

But here’s the crazy part: 46 days later, John Landy from Australia did it in 3:58.0. By year's end, three more runners beat the “impossible” 4-minute mile.

Nothing changed physically, except belief.

I love this story because whenever someone does the "impossible,” others see themselves in that someone.

“I can't" → "they did"

"They did" → "I might"

"I might" → "I will"

It's like a \textbf{possibility chain of evidence}. Of course, your "four-minute mile" might look different. Maybe it's writing that post and hitting publish. Or speaking up in meetings. Or just facing the day.

And it works both ways. You might need someone else's proof to believe in what you can do. Someone else needs your proof to believe in what they can do.

Either way, you're part of this chain.

Break your barriers. Not just for you. \\
For everyone watching who thinks they can't.

(if you like this idea, check out my visual for The Stockdale Paradox)
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to use evidence to build confidence}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-30}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
When you brainstorm visual ideas, it’s okay to be fast, messy, and even incomplete! The most important thing → get it down on paper and out of your head. I call this the \textbf{“minimum viable capture.”}

My notebooks are full of chicken scratches often filled more with words than sketches. They look like this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/bc8ec2dd10fe93f5eb178785ca1ac417.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Complaining visual (brainstorm)
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/4a65e3f32afcc0d8a5d3e310515875a4.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Stockdale Paradox (brainstorm)

And they eventually turn into this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e72e62ddd60f5ef7257bbafb15907a28.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/0910457e1f1c2e832c6e35068e4d82ed.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The point is to avoid being precious with your sketches (especially if it’s preventing you from working out the ideas in your head).

By the way, if you’re ready to take the first step to translate your ideas to visuals, Thinking in Visual Metaphors starts in a couple weeks! Enrollment closes soon!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How to use evidence to build confidence}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2025-12-30}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3a403bc6019dd17e4813c115f7060e8d.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The more efficient you get, the more you can get done, right?

But does “success” just boil down to getting the most done and as fast as possible? Hmm. Depends how you define success.

Personally, I’m burning out trying to be more efficient. So as we gear up for 2026, I’m trying something new → Slooowing dooown. I call it \textbf{“bullet-time productivity”} 😬
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
%\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/f39a268d25cc999780cd93fe634a8728.gif}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Instead of doing more, I’m \textbf{noticing more}, \textbf{feeling more}, \textbf{appreciating more}. And the number one thing I’m \textbf{loving more} is really seeing the people who’re next to me on the journey.

The older I get, the more I just want to spend every minute around the people I love.

Wishing you and yours safety and health, wondrous journeys, and well-earned time with the people who make you happiest this New Years! ❤️
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

So here’s my question this week: \textbf{What one habit (if you could could get into it) would help you be more creative?}

Reply and let me know. While I can't write back to everyone, I read every response!

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{Why you should always "root" for yourself}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-02-10}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/c5eb36cc238bc769c8705a2214504767.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A lot of people are surprised when I tell them \textbf{Twitter (not Instagram) is the first place I started posting visuals.} It’s also my “least successful” (I cringe at defining success by follower count…but let’s temporarily use this definition).

Over the last 4 years of regularly posting on X, my follower count grew to about 19,000. Nothing to complain about but half that growth happened in the first 6 months. It’s felt like a grind to grow the other half.

Then \textbf{last week something happened. }The algorithm gods in the matrix saw it fit to bring some attention to my X account probably during a perfect storm of the right person seeing the right content at the right time of day.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/c11e59208b12e6569b247bc9707c36ec.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Dec. 6, 2025 - 4 Likes
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a9547ed9a14ce5bc8235432fdd458fc7.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Feb. 5, 2026 - 16K Likes

Thankfully I learned early as a creator that social media algorithms are fickle creatures (notice that my content didn’t change, the algo did). It’s a dangerous game to measure success by their metrics. So I’ve stumbled into playing a more infinite game. The game of showing up despite the outcome.

\textbf{The 3 most important lessons I’ve learned in this game:}

You will go on a winning streak

You will go on a losing streak

You won’t know when either will stop.

And this has happened to me in every platform.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/76871455636823b53a6cfc770dfcb118.png}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How purpose is like a candle}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-02-24}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/206a6bcd11f59d99cae9e2be54ffe47b.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The biggest reason most folks believe they can’t make visual metaphors may come to you as an obvious one—\textbf{”I can’t draw.”}*

But I’ll scream this till my face is as blue as my brand colors: visual metaphors are not about pretty pictures, they’re about thinking. My friend Laura Evans said it best: “It’s not art. It’s marks with meaning.“

And the meaning doesn’t come from the graphic. Sure the pictures are a vehicle. But the passengers they deliver are the message behind the pictures.

The truth is \textbf{if you can write, you’re 70\% of the way} to crafting your own visual metaphors.

Okay. Okay. You’re right. They are called VISUAL metaphors. But the above visual is an example of how the writing is MORE important than the graphic.

Check out my Instagram comparison of the same graphic, different words:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/360af0cbadb525e1100d06f1d9eff3d5.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Feb. 21, 2025 — 1,525 Likes
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.17\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/66ce058427b0717fdd36093cf2fb5397.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Feb. 21, 2026 - 24K+ Likes

It’s true you have to understand some basic visual strategies to translate a metaphor into a visual metaphor, but if you know how to wordsmith (and if you understand that creativity is an iterative pursuit), you will stand in the top 1\% of visual creators!

\textbf{*side note:} is anyone else pissed off that A.I. has killed the human use of em-dashes?!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-02-24}

\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The myth of "being ready"}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-03-18}

{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}

\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The myth of "being ready"}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-03-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a56b1486419543093ba667336813a1d9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Last week, thanks to supporters like you, I had the privilege of running a 90min workshop at SXSW EDU called “Teaching with Visual Thinking” in Austin, TX!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/988d7c27e022d76e882a95e27c12797d.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Presenting at SXSW EDU
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/74159f0066d521522b5f328f105fa361.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The energy in the room was electric!

Speaking to a group of educators was super meaningful. Attendees came up throughout the rest of the conference to say things like this:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.13\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3f3e060b39839d8ad5411ea5c19fd9c0.jpg}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
But here's the thing. I almost didn't go for it.

When I first decided to speak at SXSW, I had a choice:

Option 1: \textbf{20min presentation} (done it before, better odds of getting in)

Option 2: \textbf{90min workshop} (4X the prep! Harder to get in)

The cohort course I teach is 3 weeks long. Choosing option 2 would mean distilling 9-hours of lessons into 90 minutes! I wasn't ready for that.

Which was exactly why I knew I had to do it.

Truth is I've spent a large part of my life waiting. Thinking if I prepped enough, I'd finally feel "ready."

It wasn't until my 40s that I finally realized the problem with thinking your way to "ready" is you don't know what you don't know. No amount of prep changes that.

Every success I've had over the last 4 years of my creator journey has come from flipping the script: \textbf{Do first, ready last.}

So learn as you go. Just in time. It's scary, sloppy, and uncomfortable. And you have to be willing to look foolish while you figure it out. But it’s far better than the alternative:

Spending your whole life in the waiting room.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The myth of "being ready"}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-03-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/9707c6525c1bd249a9cd6a918038f1b0.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Three words that change everything:\\
\textbf{"I am learning."}

It's not toxic positivity.\\
It's not pretending things are easy.\\
It's just...grace.

The same grace you'd give a friend who's trying something new.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The myth of "being ready"}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-03-18}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/0ef221e87d442ec14cc74f0c349e8624.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
\textbf{Pull the weeds.}\\
\textbf{Feed the roots.}\\
\textbf{Reap the fruits.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How emotions are like threads}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/a239411ade075a042d60ee64b2840ff9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{How emotions are like threads}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-01}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e94376b7c6316ef234743ec7dbc8988a.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
A reader asked the other week, \textbf{“How do you show adaptation?”}

One strategy is a simple line graph called \textbf{damped oscillation}. After a shock, the line swings back and forth, each arc smaller than the last, until it eventually settles in the middle.

It’s a great way to show resilience in the face of adversity (and one you can whip up on a whiteboard quickly whenever you need). For example:
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8d16d9ccd4c67d5996d4001453f22ed9.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Example of Damped Oscillation at work

The key idea is wild swings at the beginning aren't a sign that something is wrong. It’s just part of a process.

By the way if you like stuff like this, Cohort 16 of Thinking in Visual Metaphors starts in late June. Sign up for the waitlist here.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}

\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The power of mistakes and discipline}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/8d719fbe84441e7d9bbc5cb038c7c191.png}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The power of mistakes and discipline}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The gold standard of showing the power of compounding: \\
\textbf{the exponential curve.}

It’s a line that starts almost flat, growing so slowly it feels like nothing’s happening at all (this is where most people quit). But then, the sweet, sweet fruit of all that effort pays off in an “everything, everywhere, all at once” moment that pushes your results to take off!
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/e8afd1bcc58679befd1678ab97648ea7.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
One of the most famous examples of this curve comes from James Clear’s \textbf{“Atomic Habits”.}
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The power of mistakes and discipline}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ENCHANTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/56f17e095666fc73782ca7c7751b06f3.png}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The power of mistakes and discipline}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-15}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries ANALOGY}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/366138628c6e1fe03d16f46e8462031c.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
I've never regretted pausing. \\
I've regretted plenty of reactions.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The 2 types of talent}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries INTERESTING}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.55\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/7107960c2e8198a17e4cc17dbd1fa19b.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Natural talent and \textbf{Earned talent}.

Of course when you're born with traits that make you "look like a natural", you have a leg up. But if you stop there, you'll never meet your full potential.

When I was a kid, I never thought of myself as someone who could draw. I just enjoyed doing it and thought it was fun.

And you should see the visual metaphors I first posted 4 years ago! Each one took me an embarrassing amount of time and the result wasn't all that great.

But I kept at it, and after 900+ visuals…I got better! That's earned ability and something anyone can do.

It's time to earn your talent.

\textbf{* Side note:} When I posted this visual, there was meaningful dialogue around whether there is such a thing as “natural talent” in the first place. I have my own thoughts, but curious to hear what you think.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
\newpage
\renewcommand{\theposttitle}{The 2 types of talent}
\renewcommand{\thepostdate}{2026-04-29}
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
{\Huge\bfseries DESIGN}\\[6mm]
\end{center}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
The \textbf{J-Curve} (aka “the dip”) visualizes the experience of trying to do something to improve the current situation, BUT with a warning embedded in the curve: \textbf{it gets worse before it gets better. }
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{4mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/3c882e734f13cf94ac84b6d6ae8320b4.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
Notice there’s a before state, a moment of change, and an after state.

It’s important the "after" level be much HIGHER than the "before" level, instead of a return to status quo. The dip acts like a rubber band pulled down first so it can fly higher later!

The following is an example inspired by a clip from "The Curiosity Shop" with Adam Grant and Brené Brown that introduces the idea of "adaptive guilt."
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace{5mm}
\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth, height=0.24\textheight, keepaspectratio]{C:/GitHub/VisualIdeas/data/images/53d7694b6e6f14e48b2fe7d216df1d13.png}
\end{center}
\vspace{2mm}
\begin{center}
\begin{minipage}{0.92\textwidth}
\small
In this example, the J-curve shows after feeling guilty for doing a bad thing, we can self-reflect and grow into a version of ourselves that meets a higher standard of behavior.

By the way if you like stuff like this, Cohort 16 of Thinking in Visual Metaphors starts in late June. Sign up for the waitlist here.
\end{minipage}
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}
